                <p class="notranslate">

              <p class="j-desc-expand description description-expanded notranslate" itemprop="description">
                Please email hall@coreservlets.com for info on how to arrange customized courses on Java 7, Java 8, JSF 2.2, PrimeFaces, Hadoop, jQuery&#x2F;Ajax, Android programming, and other Java EE topics onsite at YOUR location.
<br />
<br />This section discusses applets and basic drawing operations. But, it also serves as an excuse to introduce general concepts that are used throughout Java programming: import statements, lifecycle methods, try&#x2F;catch blocks, and the @Override annotation. See http:&#x2F;&#x2F;courses.coreservlets.com&#x2F;Course-Materials&#x2F;java.html for the full tutorial, associated code, exercises, and exercise solutions. You can also download PDF files of each lecture, for saving or printing. Topics specific to Java 8 are covered in http:&#x2F;&#x2F;www.coreservlets.com&#x2F;java-8-tutorial&#x2F;  
              </p>

    Why Look at Applets?
&#x2022; Applets are not used very much in real life
&#x2013; Very common in early days, now mostly relegated to
relatively rare intranet applications.
&#x2022; Value
&#x2013; Natural excuse to cover other topics
&#x2022; Life-cycle methods
&#x2022; Inheritance in action
&#x2022; Import statements
&#x2022; Try/catch blocks
&#x2022; @Override
&#x2013; Chance to introduce simple graphics
&#x2022; To make exercises more interesting
&#x2013; Applets still used some in real life
&#x2022; Not so common, but not entirely gone6
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">

Applet Basics
7
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/06-java-applets-and-graphics-120913151540-phpapp02/95/java-7-and-java-8-programming-tutorial-applets-and-basic-graphics-7-638.jpg?cb=1425322067" title="View slide 7 image" target="_blank">
        7.
      </a>
    Security Restrictions:
Applets Cannot&#x2026;
&#x2022; Read from the local (client) disk
&#x2013; Applets cannot read arbitrary files
&#x2013; They can, however, instruct the browser to display pages that are
generally accessible on the Web, which might include some local
files
&#x2022; Write to the local (client) disk
&#x2013; The browser may choose to cache certain files, including some
loaded by applets, but this choice is not under direct control of the
applet
&#x2022; Open network connections other than to the
server from which the applet was loaded
&#x2013; This restriction prevents applets from browsing behind network
firewalls
8
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/06-java-applets-and-graphics-120913151540-phpapp02/95/java-7-and-java-8-programming-tutorial-applets-and-basic-graphics-8-638.jpg?cb=1425322067" title="View slide 8 image" target="_blank">
        8.
      </a>
    Applets Cannot&#x2026;
&#x2022; Link to client-side C code or call programs
installed on the browser machine
&#x2013; Ordinary Java applications can invoke locally installed programs
(Runtime.exec or ProcessBuilder.start) as well as link to local
C/C++ modules (&#x201C;native&#x201D; methods)
&#x2013; These actions are prohibited in applets because there is no way to
determine whether the operations these local programs perform are
safe
&#x2022; Discover private information about the user
&#x2013; Applets should not be able to discover the username of the person
running them or specific system information such as current users,
directory names or listings, system software, and so forth
&#x2013; However, applets can determine the name of the host they are on;
this information is already reported to the HTTP server that
delivered the applet
9
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/06-java-applets-and-graphics-120913151540-phpapp02/95/java-7-and-java-8-programming-tutorial-applets-and-basic-graphics-9-638.jpg?cb=1425322067" title="View slide 9 image" target="_blank">
        9.
      </a>
    Applet Template
import java.applet.Applet;
import java.awt.*;
public class AppletTemplate extends Applet {
// Variable declarations.
@Override // I will explain @Override later
public void init() {
// Variable initializations, image loading, etc.
}
@Override // I will explain @Override later
public void paint(Graphics g) {
// Drawing operations.
}
}
10
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/06-java-applets-and-graphics-120913151540-phpapp02/95/java-7-and-java-8-programming-tutorial-applets-and-basic-graphics-10-638.jpg?cb=1425322067" title="View slide 10 image" target="_blank">
        10.
      </a>
    Browser Caching Problems
&#x2022; Browsers normally cache applets
&#x2013; So, when you recompile applet and reload HTML page,
you still see old applet. Very annoying problem!
&#x2022; Internet Explorer and Firefox solution
&#x2013; Open Java console (see later slide) and hit &#x201C;x&#x201D;
&#x2022; Eclipse solution
&#x2013; R-click, Run As &#xF0E0; Java Applet (calls appletviewer)
&#x2022; Use this on your exercises!
&#x2013; Problem: doesn&#x2019;t use your HTML file, so you can&#x2019;t test if
the WIDTH and HEIGHT are correct. Still, convenient.
&#x2022; Appletviewer solution
&#x2013; During development, can call &#x201C;appletviewer file.html&#x201D; or
&#x201C;appletviewer http://.../file.html&#x201D; from DOS window.11
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/06-java-applets-and-graphics-120913151540-phpapp02/95/java-7-and-java-8-programming-tutorial-applets-and-basic-graphics-11-638.jpg?cb=1425322067" title="View slide 11 image" target="_blank">
        11.
      </a>
    Applet HTML Template
&lt;!DOCTYPE HTML PUBLIC "-//W3C//DTD HTML 4.0 Transitional//EN"&gt;
&lt;html&gt;
&lt;head&gt;
&lt;title&gt;A Template for Loading Applets&lt;/title&gt;
&lt;/head&gt;
&lt;body&gt;
&lt;h1&gt;A Template for Loading Applets&lt;/h1&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
&lt;applet code="AppletTemplate.class" width="120" height="60"&gt;
&lt;b&gt;Error! You must use a Java-enabled browser.&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;/applet&gt;
&lt;/body&gt;&lt;/html&gt;
12
The HTML 5 spec says to use &#x201C;object&#x201D; instead of
&#x201C;applet&#x201D;. However, &#x201C;object&#x201D; is more complex, and it
fails on multiple IE versions. So, &#x201C;applet&#x201D; is still widely
used, even with the HTML 5 DOCTYPE.
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/06-java-applets-and-graphics-120913151540-phpapp02/95/java-7-and-java-8-programming-tutorial-applets-and-basic-graphics-12-638.jpg?cb=1425322067" title="View slide 12 image" target="_blank">
        12.
      </a>
    Applet Example 1:
Drawing Diagonal Lines
import java.applet.Applet;
import java.awt.*;
/** Draws a line from top-left halfway to bottom-right. */
public class DrawLine extends Applet {
private int width; // Instance var declarations here
private int height;
@Override // I'll explain later what this optional tag does
public void init() { // Initializations here
setBackground(Color.YELLOW);
setForeground(Color.RED);
width = getWidth();
height = getHeight();
}
@Override // I'll explain later what this optional tag does
public void paint(Graphics g) { // Drawing here
g.drawLine(0, 0, width/2, height/2);
}
}13
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">

        13.

    Applet Example 2
import java.applet.Applet;
import java.awt.*;
/** An applet that draws an image. */
public class JavaJump extends Applet {
private Image jumpingJava; // Instance var declarations here
public void init() { // Initializations here
setBackground(Color.WHITE);
setFont(new Font("SansSerif", Font.BOLD, 18));
jumpingJava = getImage(getCodeBase(),
"images/Jumping-Java.gif");
add(new Label("Great Jumping Java!"));
System.out.println("Yow! I'm jiving with Java.");
}
public void paint(Graphics g) { // Drawing here
g.drawImage(jumpingJava, 0, 50, this);
}
}16
Hey! You forgot @Override and it still works. Why?
And if it works without @Override, why is @Override useful?
Good question: see upcoming slides

        17.

    Debugging Applets:
The Java Console
&#x2022; Standard output (from System.out.println) is
sent to the Java Console
&#x2013; IE6 and early releases of IE7: Tools &#xF0E0; Sun Java Console
&#x2013; Firefox, IE8+, later releases of IE7: R-click on Java icon
in taskbar, then select Console
&#x2022; In either browser, to have it
open automatically:
go to Control Panel, click on
Java, go to &#x201C;Advanced&#x201D;,
choose &#x201C;Java console&#x201D;,
and select &#x201C;Show Console&#x201D;.
&#x2013; Note that this is for your
debugging: don&#x2019;t expect end
user to ever notice this
18
Hitting &#x201C;x&#x201D; will clear cached
applets. Very useful during
development.
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/06-java-applets-and-graphics-120913151540-phpapp02/95/java-7-and-java-8-programming-tutorial-applets-and-basic-graphics-18-638.jpg?cb=1425322067" title="View slide 18 image" target="_blank">
        18.

The Value of @Override
19
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/06-java-applets-and-graphics-120913151540-phpapp02/95/java-7-and-java-8-programming-tutorial-applets-and-basic-graphics-19-638.jpg?cb=1425322067" title="View slide 19 image" target="_blank">
        19.
      </a>
    Using @Override: Quick Intro
&#x2022; Problem
public class MyApplet extends Applet
public void Paint(Graphics g) { drawSomethingCool(); }
}
&#x2022; Result: no error message, but nothing cool is drawn
&#x2022; Solution
public class MyApplet extends Applet
@Override
public void Paint(Graphics g) { drawSomethingCool(); }
}
&#x2022; Result: won&#x2019;t compile, since there is no &#x201C;Paint&#x201D; method in the
parent class that takes Graphics as an argument. Once you
change it to &#x201C;paint&#x201D;, it compiles normally.
&#x2013; You can override methods with or without @Override, but @Override
expresses design intent and also catches errors at compile time
instead of run time. (@FunctionalInterface, covered later, is similar)
20
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/06-java-applets-and-graphics-120913151540-phpapp02/95/java-7-and-java-8-programming-tutorial-applets-and-basic-graphics-20-638.jpg?cb=1425322067" title="View slide 20 image" target="_blank">
        20.
      </a>
    &#xA9; 2015 Marty Hall
Customized Java EE Training: http://courses.coreservlets.com/
Java 7, Java 8, JSF 2, PrimeFaces, Android, JSP, Ajax, jQuery, Spring MVC, RESTful Web Services, GWT, Hadoop.
Developed and taught by well-known author and developer. At public venues or onsite at your location.
Applet Life Cycle
and Methods
21
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/06-java-applets-and-graphics-120913151540-phpapp02/95/java-7-and-java-8-programming-tutorial-applets-and-basic-graphics-21-638.jpg?cb=1425322067" title="View slide 21 image" target="_blank">
        21.
      </a>
    The Applet Life Cycle
&#x2022; public void init()
&#x2013; Called when applet is first loaded into the browser.
&#x2013; Not called each time the applet is executed
&#x2022; public void start()
&#x2013; Called immediately after init initially
&#x2013; Reinvoked each time user returns to page after having left
&#x2013; Used to start animation threads
&#x2022; public void paint(Graphics g)
&#x2013; Called by the browser after init and start
&#x2013; Reinvoked whenever the browser redraws the screen
(typically when part of the screen has been obscured and
then reexposed)
&#x2013; This method is where user-level drawing is placed
22
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/06-java-applets-and-graphics-120913151540-phpapp02/95/java-7-and-java-8-programming-tutorial-applets-and-basic-graphics-22-638.jpg?cb=1425322067" title="View slide 22 image" target="_blank">
        22.
      </a>
    The Applet Life Cycle
(Continued)
&#x2022; public void stop()
&#x2013; Called when the user leaves the page
&#x2013; Used to stop animation threads
&#x2022; public void destroy()
&#x2013; Called when applet is killed by the browser
&#x2022; Nonstandard behavior in IE
&#x2013; In some versions of Internet Explorer, unlike in Firefox or
Chrome, init is called each time the user returns to the
same page, and destroy is called whenever the user leaves
the page containing the applet. I.e., applet is started over
each time (incorrect behavior!).

  </li>

        23.
      </a>
    Useful Applet Methods
&#x2022; getCodeBase, getDocumentBase
&#x2013; The URL of the:
Applet file - getCodeBase
HTML file - getDocumentBase
&#x2022; getParameter
&#x2013; Retrieves the value from the associated HTML PARAM
element
&#x2022; getWidth, getHeight
&#x2013; Returns the width/height of the applet
&#x2022; getGraphics
&#x2013; Retrieves the current Graphics object for the applet
&#x2013; The Graphics object does not persist across paint
invocations24

getAppletContext().showDocument(...)

&#x2013; Displays a string in the status line at the bottom of the

    Reading Applet Parameters
&#x2022; Use getParameter(name) to retrieve the value of
the PARAM element
&#x2013; If no match, return value is null. Always check for null!
&#x2022; The name argument is case sensitive
public void init() {
Color background = Color.GRAY;
Color foreground = Color.DARK_GRAY;
String backgroundType = getParameter("BACKGROUND");
if (backgroundType != null) {
if (backgroundType.equalsIgnoreCase("LIGHT")) {
background = Color.WHITE;
foreground = Color.BLACK;
} else if (backgroundType.equalsIgnoreCase("DARK")) {
background = Color.BLACK;
foreground = Color.WHITE;
}
}
...
}

Drawing in Applets
33
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/06-java-applets-and-graphics-120913151540-phpapp02/95/java-7-and-java-8-programming-tutorial-applets-and-basic-graphics-33-638.jpg?cb=1425322067" title="View slide 33 image" target="_blank">
        33.
      </a>
    Basic Approach
&#x2022; Ideas
&#x2013; Draw from the paint method (or, later, event handler)
&#x2013; Use a Graphics (i.e., pen) object to draw
&#x2022; In paint, you are given Graphics object. In other methods
of Applet subclass, call getGraphics() to obtain it.
&#x2013; The top-left corner is (0,0). x is to right, y is down.
&#x2022; Syntax
public void paint(Graphics g) {
g.drawLine(0, 0, 100, 100);
}
&#x2022; Draws a line from top-left corner of applet, diagonally
down and to the right.
34
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/06-java-applets-and-graphics-120913151540-phpapp02/95/java-7-and-java-8-programming-tutorial-applets-and-basic-graphics-34-638.jpg?cb=1425322067" title="View slide 34 image" target="_blank">
        34.
      </a>
    Useful Graphics Methods
&#x2022; drawString(string, left, bottom)
&#x2013; Draws a string in the current font and color with the
bottom left corner of the string at the specified location
&#x2013; One of the few methods where the y coordinate refers to
the bottom of shape, not the top. But y values are still
with respect to the top left corner of the applet window
&#x2022; drawRect(left, top, width, height)
&#x2013; Draws the outline of a rectangle (1-pixel border) in the
current color
&#x2022; fillRect(left, top, width, height)
&#x2013; Draws a solid rectangle in the current color
&#x2022; drawLine(x1, y1, x2, y2)
&#x2013; Draws a 1-pixel-thick line from (x1, y1) to (x2, y2)35
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/06-java-applets-and-graphics-120913151540-phpapp02/95/java-7-and-java-8-programming-tutorial-applets-and-basic-graphics-35-638.jpg?cb=1425322067" title="View slide 35 image" target="_blank">
        35.
      </a>
    Useful Graphics Methods
(Continued)
&#x2022; drawOval, fillOval
&#x2013; Draws an outlined and solid oval, where the arguments
describe a rectangle that bounds the oval
&#x2022; drawPolygon, fillPolygon
&#x2013; Draws an outlined and solid polygon whose points are
defined by arrays or a Polygon (a class that stores a
series of points)
&#x2013; By default, polygon is closed; to make an open polygon
use the drawPolyline method
&#x2022; drawImage
&#x2013; Draws an image
&#x2013; Images can be in JPEG or GIF (including animated GIF)
format36
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/06-java-applets-and-graphics-120913151540-phpapp02/95/java-7-and-java-8-programming-tutorial-applets-and-basic-graphics-36-638.jpg?cb=1425322067" title="View slide 36 image" target="_blank">
        36.
      </a>
    Drawing Color
&#x2022; setColor, getColor
&#x2013; Specifies the foreground color prior to drawing operation
&#x2013; By default, the graphics object receives the foreground
color of the window
&#x2022; As set via setForeground from the init() method
&#x2013; AWT has 16 predefined colors (Color.RED,
Color.BLUE, etc.) or create your own color:
new Color(r, g, b)
&#x2013; Changing the color of the Graphics object affects only
the drawing that explicitly uses that Graphics object
&#x2022; To make permanent changes, call the applet&#x2019;s
setForeground method.
37
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/06-java-applets-and-graphics-120913151540-phpapp02/95/java-7-and-java-8-programming-tutorial-applets-and-basic-graphics-37-638.jpg?cb=1425322067" title="View slide 37 image" target="_blank">
        37.
      </a>
    Graphics Font
&#x2022; setFont, getFont
&#x2013; Specifies the font to be used for drawing text
&#x2013; Determine the size of a character through
FontMetrics (in Java 2 use LineMetrics)
&#x2013; Setting the font for the Graphics object does not
persist to subsequent invocations of paint
&#x2013; Set the font of the window (I.e., call the applet&#x2019;s
setFont method) for permanent changes to the font
&#x2013; Standard Java font names: Serif (e.g., Times New
Roman), SansSerif (e.g., Arial), Monospaced
(e.g., Courier New), Dialog, and DialogInput
38
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/06-java-applets-and-graphics-120913151540-phpapp02/95/java-7-and-java-8-programming-tutorial-applets-and-basic-graphics-38-638.jpg?cb=1425322067" title="View slide 38 image" target="_blank">
        38.
      </a>
    Graphic Drawing Modes
&#x2022; setXORMode
&#x2013; Specifies a color to XOR with the color of underlying
pixel before drawing the new pixel
&#x2013; Drawing something twice in a row will restore the
original condition
&#x2022; setPaintMode
&#x2013; Set drawing mode back to normal (versus XOR)
&#x2013; Subsequent drawing will use the normal foreground color
&#x2013; Remember that the Graphics object is reset to the default
each time. So, no need to call g.setPaintMode() in paint
unless you do non-XOR drawing after your XOR drawing
39
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/06-java-applets-and-graphics-120913151540-phpapp02/95/java-7-and-java-8-programming-tutorial-applets-and-basic-graphics-39-638.jpg?cb=1425322067" title="View slide 39 image" target="_blank">
        39.
      </a>
    Drawing Diagonal Lines: Java
import java.applet.Applet;
import java.awt.*;
/** Draws a line from top-left halfway to bottom-right. */
public class DrawLine extends Applet {
private int width; // Instance var declarations here
private int height;
@Override // I'll explain later what this optional tag does
public void init() { // Initializations here
setBackground(Color.YELLOW);
setForeground(Color.RED);
width = getWidth();
height = getHeight();
}
@Override // I'll explain later what this optional tag does
public void paint(Graphics g) {
g.drawLine(0, 0, width/2, height/2);
}
}40

Loading and
Drawing Images
43
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/06-java-applets-and-graphics-120913151540-phpapp02/95/java-7-and-java-8-programming-tutorial-applets-and-basic-graphics-43-638.jpg?cb=1425322067" title="View slide 43 image" target="_blank">
        43.
      </a>
    Drawing Images
&#x2022; Register the Image (from init)
myImage = getImage(getCodeBase(), "file");
myImage = getImage(url);
&#x2013; You should declare the image as an instance variable so
that paint can access it later
&#x2022; private Image myImage;
&#x2013; Loading is done in a separate thread
&#x2013; If URL is absolute, then try/catch block is required
&#x2022; Draw the image (from paint)
g.drawImage(myImage, x, y, window);
g.drawImage(myImage, x, y, w, h, window);
&#x2013; May draw partial image or nothing at all
&#x2013; Use the applet (this) for the window argument44
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/06-java-applets-and-graphics-120913151540-phpapp02/95/java-7-and-java-8-programming-tutorial-applets-and-basic-graphics-44-638.jpg?cb=1425322067" title="View slide 44 image" target="_blank">
        44.
      </a>
    Loading Applet Image from
Relative URL
import java.applet.Applet;
import java.awt.*;
/** An applet that loads an image from a relative URL. */
public class JavaMan1 extends Applet {
private Image javaMan;
@Override
public void init() {
javaMan = getImage(getCodeBase(),
"images/Java-Man.gif");
}
@Override
public void paint(Graphics g) {
g.drawImage(javaMan, 0, 0, this);
}
}45
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/06-java-applets-and-graphics-120913151540-phpapp02/95/java-7-and-java-8-programming-tutorial-applets-and-basic-graphics-45-638.jpg?cb=1425322067" title="View slide 45 image" target="_blank">

      </a>
    Image Loading Result
46
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/06-java-applets-and-graphics-120913151540-phpapp02/95/java-7-and-java-8-programming-tutorial-applets-and-basic-graphics-46-638.jpg?cb=1425322067" title="View slide 46 image" target="_blank">
        46.
      </a>
    Loading Applet Image from
Absolute URL
import java.applet.Applet;
import java.awt.*;
import java.net.*;
...
private Image javaMan;
@Override
public void init() {
try {
URL imageFile =
new URL("http://www.corewebprogramming.com" +
"/images/Java-Man.gif");
javaMan = getImage(imageFile);
} catch(MalformedURLException mue) {
showStatus("Bogus image URL.");
System.out.println("Bogus URL");
}
}
47
In real life, it is not useful to load images from absolute URLs in applets. That is because the browser security rules mandate that the applet can only connect
back to the machine it was loaded from. But, since we are covering image loading anyhow, it is worth mentioning this because you use this approach when
loading images in regular desktop applications (not browser-based applets). Besides, this gives me an excuse to cover try/catch blocks now.

        47.
      </a>

Basic Try/Catch Blocks
(More Features in Section on File IO)
48
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/06-java-applets-and-graphics-120913151540-phpapp02/95/java-7-and-java-8-programming-tutorial-applets-and-basic-graphics-48-638.jpg?cb=1425322067" title="View slide 48 image" target="_blank">
        48.
      </a>
    Aside: Exceptions and
try/catch Blocks
&#x2022; Error-handling system is based on exceptions
&#x2013; Exceptions handled in a try/catch block
&#x2013; When an exception occurs, process flow is immediately transferred
to the catch block
&#x2013; Most exceptions must be handled (unlike C++). If API says method
or constructor throws exception, code won&#x2019;t compile unless you use
try/catch or say the method throws exception
&#x2022; Basic form
try {
statement1;
statement2;
...
} catch(SomeExceptionClass someVar) {
handleTheException(someVar);
}
49
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/06-java-applets-and-graphics-120913151540-phpapp02/95/java-7-and-java-8-programming-tutorial-applets-and-basic-graphics-49-638.jpg?cb=1425322067" title="View slide 49 image" target="_blank">
        49.
      </a>
    More Info
50
One Catch Multiple Catches Throwing
try {
statement1;
statement2;
...
} catch(Eclass var) {
doBlah(var);
}
Run all statements in try block. If
everything finishes normally, you
are done. If an exception of type
Eclass occurs, jump down to
catch block.
try {
statement1;
statement2;
...
} catch(Eclass1 var1) {
...
} catch(Eclass2 var2) {
...
} catch(Eclass3 var3) {
...
}
First matching catch fires, so
exceptions should be ordered from
most specific to most general
&#x2022; Due to inheritance, more than one
match is possible
public void foo()
throws Eclass1 {
&#x2026;
}
Instead of catching exception here,
throw it to the calling code, which
must catch the exception or throw it
further.
Covered in later lecture on File IO: finally blocks [&#x2026;catch(&#x2026;){&#x2026;}finally{&#x2026;}], multicatch [catch(E1|E2 e)], and try with resources [try(BufferedReader reader&#x2026;) {&#x2026;} &#x2026;]
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/06-java-applets-and-graphics-120913151540-phpapp02/95/java-7-and-java-8-programming-tutorial-applets-and-basic-graphics-50-638.jpg?cb=1425322067" title="View slide 50 image" target="_blank">
        50.
      </a>
    Preview of Topics Covered in
File IO Lecture
&#x2022; Covered here:
basics
try {
statement1;
statement2;
...
} catch(Eclass1 var1) {
...
} catch(Eclass2 var2) {
...
} catch(Eclass3 var3) {
...
}
&#x2026;
&#x2022; New: finally
try {&#x2026;
} catch(&#x2026;) {&#x2026;
} finally {
&#x2026;
}
&#x2022; New: multicatch
try {&#x2026;
} catch(Eclass1 | Eclass e) {
&#x2026;
} &#x2026;
&#x2022; New: try with resources
try (SomeAutoCloseable var = &#x2026;) {&#x2026;
} catch(&#x2026;) { &#x2026;
} &#x2026;
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/06-java-applets-and-graphics-120913151540-phpapp02/95/java-7-and-java-8-programming-tutorial-applets-and-basic-graphics-51-638.jpg?cb=1425322067" title="View slide 51 image" target="_blank">
        51.
      </a>
    &#xA9; 2015 Marty Hall
Customized Java EE Training: http://courses.coreservlets.com/
Java 7, Java 8, JSF 2, PrimeFaces, Android, JSP, Ajax, jQuery, Spring MVC, RESTful Web Services, GWT, Hadoop.
Developed and taught by well-known author and developer. At public venues or onsite at your location.
Advanced Topics(These topics are specific to GUI programs. Skip this section if you are planning on only
doing server-side apps and are using this lecture only to learn general topics like try/catch
blocks, @Override, lifecycle methods, import statements, and so forth.)
52
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/06-java-applets-and-graphics-120913151540-phpapp02/95/java-7-and-java-8-programming-tutorial-applets-and-basic-graphics-52-638.jpg?cb=1425322067" title="View slide 52 image" target="_blank">
        52.
      </a>
    Controlling Image Loading
&#x2022; Use prepareImage to start loading image
prepareImage(image, window)
prepareImage(image, width, height, window)
&#x2013; Starts loading image immediately (on separate thread),
instead of when needed by drawImage
&#x2013; Particularly useful if the images will not be drawn until
the user initiates some action such as clicking on a button
or choosing a menu option
&#x2013; Since the applet thread immediately continues execution
after the call to prepareImage, the image may not be
completely loaded before paint is reached
53
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/06-java-applets-and-graphics-120913151540-phpapp02/95/java-7-and-java-8-programming-tutorial-applets-and-basic-graphics-53-638.jpg?cb=1425322067" title="View slide 53 image" target="_blank">
        53.
      </a>
    Controlling Image Loading,
Case I: No prepareImage
&#x2022; Image is not loaded over network until after
Display Image is pressed. 30.4 seconds.
54
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/06-java-applets-and-graphics-120913151540-phpapp02/95/java-7-and-java-8-programming-tutorial-applets-and-basic-graphics-54-638.jpg?cb=1425322067" title="View slide 54 image" target="_blank">
        54.
      </a>
    Controlling Image Loading,
Case 2: With prepareImage
&#x2022; Image loaded over network immediately.
0.05 seconds after pressing button.
55
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/06-java-applets-and-graphics-120913151540-phpapp02/95/java-7-and-java-8-programming-tutorial-applets-and-basic-graphics-55-638.jpg?cb=1425322067" title="View slide 55 image" target="_blank">
        55.
      </a>
    Controlling Image Loading:
MediaTracker
&#x2022; Registering images with a MediaTracker to
control image loading
MediaTracker tracker = new MediaTracker(this);
tracker.addImage(image1, 0);
tracker.addImage(image2, 1);
try {
tracker.waitForAll();
} catch(InterruptedException ie) {}
if (tracker.isErrorAny()) {
System.out.println("Error while loading image");
}
&#x2013; Applet thread will block until all images are loaded
&#x2013; Each image is loaded in parallel on a separate thread
56
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/06-java-applets-and-graphics-120913151540-phpapp02/95/java-7-and-java-8-programming-tutorial-applets-and-basic-graphics-56-638.jpg?cb=1425322067" title="View slide 56 image" target="_blank">
        56.
      </a>
    Useful MediaTracker Methods
&#x2022; addImage
&#x2013; Register a normal or scaled image with a given ID
&#x2022; checkAll, checkID
&#x2013; Checks whether all or a particular registered image is
done loading
&#x2022; isErrorAny, isErrorID
&#x2013; Indicates if any or a particular image encountered an error
while loading
&#x2022; waitForAll, waitForID
&#x2013; Start loading all images or a particular image
&#x2013; Method does not return (blocks) until image is loaded
&#x2022; See TrackerUtil in book for simplified
usage of MediaTracker
57
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/06-java-applets-and-graphics-120913151540-phpapp02/95/java-7-and-java-8-programming-tutorial-applets-and-basic-graphics-57-638.jpg?cb=1425322067" title="View slide 57 image" target="_blank">
        57.
      </a>
    Loading Images,
Case I: No MediaTracker
&#x2022; Image size is wrong, since the image won&#x2019;t be
done loading, and &#x2013;1 will be returned
@Overrride
public void init() {
image = getImage(getDocumentBase(), imageName);
imageWidth = image.getWidth(this);
imageHeight = image.getHeight(this);
}
@Override
public void paint(Graphics g) {
g.drawImage(image, 0, 0, this);
g.drawRect(0, 0, imageWidth, imageHeight);
}
58
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/06-java-applets-and-graphics-120913151540-phpapp02/95/java-7-and-java-8-programming-tutorial-applets-and-basic-graphics-58-638.jpg?cb=1425322067" title="View slide 58 image" target="_blank">
        58.
      </a>
    Loading Images,
Case 2: With MediaTracker
&#x2022; Image is loaded before determining size
@Override
public void init() {
image = getImage(getDocumentBase(), imageName);
MediaTracker tracker = new MediaTracker(this);
tracker.addImage(image, 0);
try {
tracker.waitForAll();
} catch(InterruptedException ie) {}
...
imageWidth = image.getWidth(this);
imageHeight = image.getHeight(this);
}
@Override
public void paint(Graphics g) {
g.drawImage(image, 0, 0, this);
g.drawRect(0, 0, imageWidth, imageHeight);
}59

        61.
      </a>
    Summary: General Topics
&#x2022; Use try/catch blocks to handle exceptions
try {
...
} catch(Eclass1 var1) { ...
} catch(Eclass2 var2) { ...
} catch(Eclass3 var3) { ...
}
&#x2013; More features of try/catch blocks in upcoming lecture (File IO)
&#x2022; Always use @Override when replacing
methods from parent class
&#x2013; Catches typos at compile time
&#x2022; If does not match, code will not compile
&#x2013; Expresses design intent
&#x2022; I.e., tells fellow developers that this is method from parent62
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/06-java-applets-and-graphics-120913151540-phpapp02/95/java-7-and-java-8-programming-tutorial-applets-and-basic-graphics-62-638.jpg?cb=1425322067" title="View slide 62 image" target="_blank">
        62.
      </a>
    Summary:
Applet-Specific Topics
&#x2022; Applet operations are restricted
&#x2013; Applet cannot read/write local files, call local programs,
or connect to any host other than the one from which it
was loaded
&#x2022; The init method
&#x2013; Called only when applet loaded, not each time executed
&#x2013; This is where you use getParameter to read param data
&#x2022; The paint method
&#x2013; Called each time applet is displayed
&#x2013; Coordinates in drawing operations are wrt top-left corner
&#x2022; Drawing images
&#x2013; getImage(getCodeBase(), "imageFile") to &#x201C;load&#x201D; image
&#x2013; g.drawImage(image, x, y, this) to draw image
63
 
  </li>

        63.
